  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6c6835b8-10ac-4034-948d-998adfabb2c4'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4127786141027194413">An international bestseller with tremendous word-of-mouth appeal, "Follow Your Heart" is a bittersweet, heartwarming novel spanning generations and teaching the universal truths about life, love, and what lies within each of us. Originally published in Italy, "Follow Your Heart" won the coveted Premio Donna Citta di Roma and sold over 800,000 copies in that country alone b</span>
  <span id="freeText4127786141027194413" style="display:none">An international bestseller with tremendous word-of-mouth appeal, "Follow Your Heart" is a bittersweet, heartwarming novel spanning generations and teaching the universal truths about life, love, and what lies within each of us. Originally published in Italy, "Follow Your Heart" won the coveted Premio Donna Citta di Roma and sold over 800,000 copies in that country alone before hitting bestseller lists throughout the rest of Europe. Now North American readers can enjoy the novel that has won over the world.<br /><br />It begins in late autumn 1992 as an elderly Italian woman, prompted by the knowledge of her encroaching death, sits down to write a letter to her granddaughter now grown and living in far-off America. Through these moving reflections, we see one life laid bare--joys, sorrows, regrets, and all. And through the eyes of a woman nearing the end of her days, we come to understand what life experience has taught her: that no matter what the stakes, we must look within ourselves and gather the courage to follow our hearts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4127786141027194413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_578488848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/578488848" />
    <a title="Kari Kaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18975506-kari-kaz"><img alt="Kari Kaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478381898p2/18975506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/578488848?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kari Kaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kari Kaz" href="/user/show/18975506-kari-kaz">Kari Kaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18975506-kari-kaz?shelf=susp-mys-drama">susp-mys-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18975506-kari-kaz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578488848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12867002267910232753">This is one of those books that stays with you long after you finish reading it. It is hard to place it in a category since it deals with love, life, forgiveness, acceptance and understanding. The author conveys her messages through letters written from a grandmother to her cynical granddaughter. She tries to make her see that we are all threads linked together in a bigger picture, and the importance of listening to what is inside of you. She uses wonderful imagery and her observations may apply</span>
  <span id="freeText12867002267910232753" style="display:none">This is one of those books that stays with you long after you finish reading it. It is hard to place it in a category since it deals with love, life, forgiveness, acceptance and understanding. The author conveys her messages through letters written from a grandmother to her cynical granddaughter. She tries to make her see that we are all threads linked together in a bigger picture, and the importance of listening to what is inside of you. She uses wonderful imagery and her observations may apply to you at different points in your life. I think this is one of those books you either love or dislike completely, depending on your frame of mind when you read it. Her style is somewhat poetic and poignant but her messages come across clearly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12867002267910232753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101038572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7188754258177627168">This book is deeply moving because it deals so closely with issues close to the human heart. The prose is simple and uplifting, the story just an excuse to reveal to us universal truths that we all know but refuse to acknowledge. Critical and cynical people might brush this book aside but I feel that one really has to look very deeply into it to really discover its true worth. This must be read with an open mind and I feel that the ending is particularly apt because there is none. This situation</span>
  <span id="freeText7188754258177627168" style="display:none">This book is deeply moving because it deals so closely with issues close to the human heart. The prose is simple and uplifting, the story just an excuse to reveal to us universal truths that we all know but refuse to acknowledge. Critical and cynical people might brush this book aside but I feel that one really has to look very deeply into it to really discover its true worth. This must be read with an open mind and I feel that the ending is particularly apt because there is none. This situation could be so easily applied to our daily lives and the author is telling us in simple gracious terms that patience and undersanding should be the forefront of our relationship with our family. Despite the somewhat muddled use of the flashback technique and several narratives that are a little to rambling, this is a jewel that teaches love, in a world where there is little to be found. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2941176723912751122">This is the brutally honest letter a grandmother who is nearing death writes to the granddaughter she raised alone. Her granddaughter is obviously a headstrong young woman who has moved to America leaving her grandmother in Italy heartbroken and alone. <br/><br/>The grandmother can feel death coming and wants to leave her granddaughter a letter of history and hope for the future. She pulls no punches. She is not afraid to illuminate her own shortcomings as well as those around her, granddaughter included.</span>
  <span id="freeText2941176723912751122" style="display:none">This is the brutally honest letter a grandmother who is nearing death writes to the granddaughter she raised alone. Her granddaughter is obviously a headstrong young woman who has moved to America leaving her grandmother in Italy heartbroken and alone. <br /><br />The grandmother can feel death coming and wants to leave her granddaughter a letter of history and hope for the future. She pulls no punches. She is not afraid to illuminate her own shortcomings as well as those around her, granddaughter included. It is difficult to read that she did not think about her daughter for several years after her death or that she did not love her daughter enough without your heart breaking a little. This is a woman who was not going to spare her granddaughter the truth.<br /><br />I was pulled in right from the beginning. It was real and honest and a great story of three generations of women who all seemed to be fighting the past. It is definitely a worthwhile read.<br /></span>

<div id="review_592453285" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592453285" />
    <a title="Alisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5167342-alisha"><img alt="Alisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308762259p2/5167342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592453285?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisha" href="/user/show/5167342-alisha">Alisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592453285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1251569070753900140">-Every now and then we saw one (firework) that exploded before it got very high. Well, whenever I think about my mother's life, or my grandmother's, or the lives of so many people I know, that's the image that comes to mind~fireworks that fizzled down in the lower altitudes instead of climbing up to the sky.<br/><br/>-Though you may not know it, your whole life and the lives of those close to you are at stake when you choose whether to go straight or turn aside.<br/><br/>-This (religion) is one of those areas where</span>
  <span id="freeText1251569070753900140" style="display:none">-Every now and then we saw one (firework) that exploded before it got very high. Well, whenever I think about my mother's life, or my grandmother's, or the lives of so many people I know, that's the image that comes to mind~fireworks that fizzled down in the lower altitudes instead of climbing up to the sky.<br /><br />-Though you may not know it, your whole life and the lives of those close to you are at stake when you choose whether to go straight or turn aside.<br /><br />-This (religion) is one of those areas where you can't push or pull too hard, otherwise the same thing happens to you as happens to street vendors: the more they hustle their products, the more the whole thing seems like a hoax.<br /><br />-I didn't want to be calm, I didn't want anything to dull my grief.<br /><br />-Do you know what's one mistake we always make? Believing that life's immutable, that once you get on a particular track you have to follow it to the end of the line.<br /><br />-With the absolute conviction of adolescence, you believed that the unhappiness tormenting you then would torment you forever.<br /><br />-The voice of appearances was appealing to you on one side, the voice of the heart on the other, and without any doubt, without any hesitation, you chose the heart. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1251569070753900140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1974332741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5430063998608144738">The perfect antidote for recovering from the flu. I felt so absorbed by this Italian woman's reflection upon her life that I didn't feel as though I was wasting my time healing. It is her final gift for her granddaughter, the unsealing of secrets, the sharing of what is closest to her heart, and her acceptance of the time at hand. Part inspiration, her final letter is crafted with honesty, love, insight, and humility. It absorbed me as if I were sitting in her garden with a cup of coffee while s</span>
  <span id="freeText5430063998608144738" style="display:none">The perfect antidote for recovering from the flu. I felt so absorbed by this Italian woman's reflection upon her life that I didn't feel as though I was wasting my time healing. It is her final gift for her granddaughter, the unsealing of secrets, the sharing of what is closest to her heart, and her acceptance of the time at hand. Part inspiration, her final letter is crafted with honesty, love, insight, and humility. It absorbed me as if I were sitting in her garden with a cup of coffee while sharing remembrances. I read it through in one sitting. Now I'm putting it in the mail to share with another friend whom I have shared this life's journey. Pass it on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5430063998608144738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El Ko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El Ko" href="/user/show/42208672-el-ko">El Ko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597466987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17486054288552289235">Where are your eyes?<br/><br/>In my opinion this book is tragic. Because everything that happened isn´t really anyones fault but every character must face nearly unbearable consequenses. The letters are heartwarming and are full of wisdom of a person who seems to have seen it all. And I kept wondering: where are Olgas eyes? The main characters eyes seem to notice what seems to be invisible for so many of us. They wander around and seem to understand a thousand stories in a tree. <br/>What is really interesting</span>
  <span id="freeText17486054288552289235" style="display:none">Where are your eyes?<br /><br />In my opinion this book is tragic. Because everything that happened isn´t really anyones fault but every character must face nearly unbearable consequenses. The letters are heartwarming and are full of wisdom of a person who seems to have seen it all. And I kept wondering: where are Olgas eyes? The main characters eyes seem to notice what seems to be invisible for so many of us. They wander around and seem to understand a thousand stories in a tree. <br />What is really interesting about this book is that since it is from the perspective of a woman who is just about to die you just somehow see your life from another perspective.<br /><br />However, while Olga is in fact wise, i must say that I often disagree with the authors tone. Sometimes she sounds like she has not only seen it all but also understands everything which is simply not true. <br />To be honest, I am in fact one of those who see the heart as muscle. Well, maybe more, but from a scientific point of view it all happens in your mind. All your feelings, your paths. But I don´t think that it was the books intention to attract the reasonable part of us. She adressed our hearts.<br /><br />But since I am familiar with a southern language, just as Tamaros mothertongue (Italian) I understand that the way she articulates certain thoughts may sound somehow strange or unfamiliar to the westernized world.<br /><br />At the end of the day it is still a lovely book, that opens up your mind, and also your heart because it somehow forces you to "look inside". </span>
  <a data-text-id="17486054288552289235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2698087282981265564" style="display:none">“And later on, when so many roads open up before you, you don't know which to take, don't pick one at random; sit down and wait. Breathe deeply, trustingly, the way you breathed on the day when you came into the world, don't let anything distract you, wait and wait some more. Stay still, be quiet, and listen to your heart. Then, when it speaks, get up and go where it takes you.”<br />It is the explicit of the novel, which is obviously a love story, but also the story of a search of the original home background, of the family, conducted with the desire to take back your own life mixed to the feeling of revulsion and anger for the environment and for the family in which you are living, but without having the ability to find the center of your interests.<br />The Flaubertian style of the story let the narration flow as rhythmic and musical as a poem, in which the emotions and feelings are intensely bright, where despite the reason has not a fundamental role, it becomes the excuse, just a little plausible, to legitimize the reasons of the heart, reasons that reason does not know, according to a well-known thought of Pascal.<br />It is an unputdownable book and it's definitely the best book of Susanna Tamaro, I got the book after the film by Cristina Comencini, that I really liked, broadcast by RAI in 2014 in memory of Virna Lisi.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193821616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13408894107083128214">The bestselling epistolary novel <i>Follow Your Heart</i> by Italian writer Susanna Tamaro gives account of over eighty years in the life of Olga. After a heart-attack the old woman who lives alone in her house in Trieste in Northern Italy feels the need to re-evaluate her past and to set things right with her nameless granddaughter in America before it’s too late. She writes a series of twelve letters to the young woman whom she raised and who left unhappy, angry and confused because too much had rema</span>
  <span id="freeText13408894107083128214" style="display:none">The bestselling epistolary novel <i>Follow Your Heart</i> by Italian writer Susanna Tamaro gives account of over eighty years in the life of Olga. After a heart-attack the old woman who lives alone in her house in Trieste in Northern Italy feels the need to re-evaluate her past and to set things right with her nameless granddaughter in America before it’s too late. She writes a series of twelve letters to the young woman whom she raised and who left unhappy, angry and confused because too much had remained unsaid between them. At last, as a kind of late confession and spiritual legacy, Olga breaks her silence and reveals to her granddaughter not just her entire life with its many ups and downs but also her scarred soul encouraging the young woman to always follow her heart – unlike herself. <br /><br />Be invited to <a href="http://edith-lagraziana.blogspot.com/2013/03/follow-your-heart-by-susanna-tamaro.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>click here</b>
</a> and read the long review of the book that I published on my book blog <a href="http://edith-lagraziana.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Edith's Miscellany</i>
</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1034997550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1034997550" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12253407135346889614">From the title I thought it was going to be a simple romance novel. … No. An elderly woman in Italy is contemplating her coming death. She is alone except for an old dog that had belonged to her granddaughter. She had raised her granddaughter from the time the child was 3. At the time of her daughter’s death in a car accident, she had been estranged from her daughter for several years. Now her granddaughter, with whom she had a rocky relationship, is in her early 20s and has gone to America to “</span>
  <span id="freeText12253407135346889614" style="display:none">From the title I thought it was going to be a simple romance novel. … No. An elderly woman in Italy is contemplating her coming death. She is alone except for an old dog that had belonged to her granddaughter. She had raised her granddaughter from the time the child was 3. At the time of her daughter’s death in a car accident, she had been estranged from her daughter for several years. Now her granddaughter, with whom she had a rocky relationship, is in her early 20s and has gone to America to “find herself.” The woman does some serious soul-searching, and decides that she must tell her granddaughter some truths about her family, even though it will hurt. She does not want to interrupt her granddaughter’s life, so decides to write a series of letters to her granddaughter who will find them after her death. In these letters she explains what her life was like and how it affected herself, her daughter, and now her granddaughter. She hopes that in telling her tale, the granddaughter can be free of the guilt that has guided the grandmother’s life. Very philosophical! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12253407135346889614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8087277236090886679" style="display:none">This quote is making some days of mine!<br /><br />''Every time you feel lost, confused, think about trees, remember how they grow. Remember that a tree with lots of branches and few roots will get toppled by the first strong wind, while the sap hardly moves in a tree with many roots and few branches. Roots and branches must grow in equal measure, you have to stand both inside of things and above them, because only then will you be able to offer shade and shelter, only then will you be able to cover yourself with leaves and fruit at the proper season.<br /><br />And later on, when so many roads open up before you, you don't know which to take, don't pick one at random; sit down and wait. Breathe deeply, trustingly, the way you breathed on the day when you came into the world, don't let anything distract you, wait and wait some more. Stay still, be quiet, and listen to your heart. Then, when it speaks, get up and go where it takes you.''</span>

  <span id="freeText6980683867216451760" style="display:none">I borrowed this book from a friend and refused to give it back. I reluctantly returned it only for my friend to give it to me as a present shortly afterwards as I could not find it in print. A grandmother, feeling that her last days are quickly approaching, starts writing a long letter to her granddaughter in the form of a diary. what starts as a review of the events of the day and her relationship with the granddaughter which at the time of the girls departure (to America, to study) seems to have been quite haphazard, slowly becomes a reflection on life (the writer's life and life in general). The experiences, advice and pearls of wisdom that constitute this reflection can be applied to any person's life. If anything, I found that the end arrived too suddenly.</span>

I was able to look back at my time in Veneto, Italy with fond memories as the story was set in the same region and where the lifestyle is described as "Dolce far Niente," "the sweetness of doing nothing." The story is written as a letter from a dying grandmother to her nearly estranged granddaughter. The Grandmother tells her story, love, life, and tragedy.   <span id="freeText15289017369893247468" style="display:none">Lovely little story with plenty of heart-advice and good reminders. I was able to look back at my time in Veneto, Italy with fond memories as the story was set in the same region and where the lifestyle is described as "Dolce far Niente," "the sweetness of doing nothing." The story is written as a letter from a dying grandmother to her nearly estranged granddaughter. The Grandmother tells her story, love, life, and tragedy. She talks about her daughter who tragically dies in a car accident (the granddaughter's mother) and gives some explanation for her choices in life, along with some regrets and things she wishes she would have done differently. Ultimately, the message is to follow your heart and not forget the things that matter the most in life. Very nice read. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12309040204481413951">I was needing a book that make me feel closer to my mom in Heaven, and I found this book. My mother always said I should read this book, she said it was wonderful. A recomendation from her is something you better not miss.<br/>A long letter from a grandmother to her grandaughter. If you wish a long confession of how she feels in the nightfall of her life. Intimate, profound, with the feeling on the skin, anyone can feel related to it.<br/> I really like it. Of course, it made me cry in many parts, special</span>
  <span id="freeText12309040204481413951" style="display:none">I was needing a book that make me feel closer to my mom in Heaven, and I found this book. My mother always said I should read this book, she said it was wonderful. A recomendation from her is something you better not miss.<br />A long letter from a grandmother to her grandaughter. If you wish a long confession of how she feels in the nightfall of her life. Intimate, profound, with the feeling on the skin, anyone can feel related to it.<br /> I really like it. Of course, it made me cry in many parts, specially the ones where I could imagine my mother talking, even when her personal story was very different from the woman of the book. A must read book for everyone.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cP3oKa4LKvFCgtZoa9EH6FtK0CiyRJvWD0UouS5Afszd1GUMOEeu2HVESUQS4+WWb18glNHkflRIZIHGILP71w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QjgDCuDHQljCDgabH8EU4jHZpukaU6AQIiOdxH60tpTvEY4vdovGcfXImbdm8/acBcxWVXnzRZJlAjS7cEczjw==')})
  }

Immergendosi nella sofferenza e superandola, ci ricorda come sia sempre possibile buttarsi alle spalle la sfiducia per andare al di là dei nostri limiti. Massimo Gramellini ha raccolto gli slanci e le ferite di una vita priva del suo appiglio più solido. Una lotta incessante contro la solitudine, l\'inadeguatezza e il senso di abbandono, raccontata con passione e delicata ironia. La luce si è ritirata verso qualche luogo nel cielo. Il buio della notte avvolge le viuzze del paese e il mare è nero come la pece. Julia ha perso la strada di casa: è circondata dal silenzio e sente solo la voce del vento che soffia dal mare, e profuma di sale e di fiori. Non ricorda cosa sia successo: era uscita a prendere del latte per suo figlio, ma sulla strada del ritorno all\'improvviso si è ritrovata in macchina senza soldi, documenti e cellulare. Prova a contattarli da un telefono pubblico, ma la linea è sempre occupata. Tutto, intorno a lei, è così familiare eppure così stranamente irreale. Tra le vie oscure e labirintiche c\'è solo una luce, quella di un locale notturno. A Julia non resta altra scelta che raggiungerlo, nella speranza di trovare qualcuno che l\'aiuti. Qui, quasi ad aspettarla, c\'è un uomo, un tipo affascinante, con la barba incolta e l\'accento dell\'Est Europa, che sembra sapere tante, troppe cose su di lei. Si chiama Marcus: Julia ha la sensazione di averlo già incontrato da qualche parte. Fidarsi di lui è facile. Eppure Marcus non è quello che sembra e nasconde qualcosa, come ha appena scoperto anche Félix, che sta cercando in tutti i modi di riavere Julia con sé. Ma la donna può affidarsi solo a sé stessa. Deve ascoltare il vento che continua a soffiare intorno a lei. Deve capire cosa sta accadendo. Perché è lì, nel suo istinto di sopravvivenza, che può trovare finalmente la strada di casa. Dopo l\'incredibile successo del Profumo delle foglie di limone, un fenomeno editoriale unico, ancora nella classifica dei bestseller a un anno dall\'uscita, Clara Sánchez torna con un romanzo dalla forza dirompente. <span id="freeTextContainer8269653859985966841">Susanna Tamaro is an Italian novelist.<br/><br/>Her second novel <i>Per voce sola</i> (Just For One Voice) won the <b>International PEN Award</b> and was translated into several languages.<br/><br/>Her novel <i>Va' dove ti porta il cuore</i> (Follow your Heart) was an international bestseller and became the "Italian book most sold in the 20th century".</span>
